Viewable Unimpressive


The debate over the value of viewable impressions as a metric for online branding campaigns is endless at the moment. Following the Media Ratings Council's preliminary conclusion that viewable impressions aren't all that viewable right now, Mitch Weinstein, SVP, director of Ad Operations at Universal McCann, writing on the shop's blog, offers what he calls "the agency perspective" on the whole thing. While he sees viewable impressions eventually becoming the "cornerstone of the industry," there's a lot of complexity until the ground is actually broken. "Until such time where methodologies and technologies become more consistent through audits and certifications, it will be difficult to use the Viewable count as the basis for billing. In the meantime, the publishers and agencies getting an early jump on the technology will set the pace and tone for the rest of the industry." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3K8stgXfOPxs9rXODzugOCFu29TCZBfhAgny-ezYIYmlmsYjFUA40GA4j85Tewa_XilT-tuBP2TSH_5Kd3CoPDHZPiGR7TGDVKmTnRpLfV5aRCNZ42YGgOzLJBUu1TwB8trKkR9mWlogAAwfTLcesOeV_GmVJLxZYs=> . 


Speak to the Marketer


The ad tech ecosystem is way too obsessed with buying mechanisms and price, Digilant CEO Ed Montes writes in a Mediapost column. "It's imperative for marketers to understand that today's RTB and programmatic environments are immature, with significantly too much focus placed on bidding and price rather than marketing and communication outcomes." More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3JgfTL5yiFVg_uowIZyfRp93moqaAlZTAZtVrb0b6a-XnKVpGqE9vcXYMUdpgqU5Kzo5s0l0Y4GFtRGF0SFwhWMJgDQtB5bcSYY3Um3ow0U6cUQheSWy4TR3tUZU3MuEqSheANx4uhtR9D0HuWwikqZptzzUvadvoekCBgWEhSYyFaQ1_YFMVHnuRJ4fG9rzG0=> 


Commenting On Tags


The IAB wants You. That is if you want to provide a comment on best practices for site tagging and "alleviate industry-wide complexities." A helpful list of pain points are identified that publishers are managing today: "User abandonment; Negative customer experience; Performance impact; Operational strain; Unintended transfer of data; Privacy issues." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3KU9GL2HoPJDexKyiIybbVUpFvefV9Tva76UCc3BuM7qsVR0Q173_mGoWN3KeKSum7AMsJi-clQmHb13YfZ56cvlPlLNemU2Fyv_ZlfZ2Yb1hUI-cR-UIyjjXzES1Ix8nKxBqjtcCAlMVhSaNku9WPf6mrKPEpct4HgM41ikaSbAoS55j-VgnonaTlser_NiBRRymcpd7yABdoZRNbcT3R0> . And, see the site tagging site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3IjybvOPDlqRkxm9LmlswIrJKZGiVCLS28iOEExsAcBhIvNt4QsCICNoxlYqpddVxpwM_bF_WRlFw-rEvaL-BoHa1K8waAD1Q10ugFl_Ibf1FBpEit_p_M4> . 


Testing Direct Sales


On Digiday, Brian Morrissey asks industry execs if Federated Media's move away from direct sales for display and toward programmatic is a pivotal moment for the industry at-large. Tremor's head seller Jason Krebs is non-plussed as he says, "It doesn't matter what program digital marketers are actually buying as 80 percent of all dollars are being used to deliver more friends, fans, tweets, followers, likes, shares, views or clicks." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3IDeEy6so1loOKoIaaTj1-G7lPb3aYYlaL8YS-I6DLkwOQxCHox5CE2SVXT3zCCv2HUcq7LAneX9I1NVc0nvzL4XG4UmE_9Hqdgi_mPdLwPU9Z89vD-XKERPWo28k9ak-MWyLfDi1BuNt006rlNIAAWO5OCowfymnnHwXLO1qSo1A==>  


Facebook Vs Google, Round 384


On Wired, Google social VP Bradley Horowitz takes a few swings at Facebook as Google amps up its competition with the social giant. Horowitz tells Wired, "We launched to a lot of skepticism and I will be the first to admit in the wake of Orkut and Blogger and Buzz and Wave, the world had a right to be skeptical about Google. When we said this was different, people didn't necessarily believe us.... What I think has happened in the intervening year [is] the world has changed a lot. And whereas a year ago, we may have been accused of wanting to be Facebook, it's clear to the world now that Google would not want that outcome..." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3L-Hl6mPRGYGS8-YH7_IIRNoCAHwf64KbFEo0KZaYtewdtz6UqDSTPe3OKehxG2TymxJAOO7ItOUlGLfDk-_SK0KXcmfodiWZfbDErwU1ca-ElJAjoWWwzxQFIobcKld39zMqz-fxix9GN_edD5qbXNUy7jDgpYyLY=>

Aegis' China Deal


It's getting harder for Western media shops to find scalable digital agencies in China to acquire, but Aegis has been able to snap up OMP, one of that country's few remaining large independents. OMP will be connected with Aegis' search specialist shop Isobar. "OMP is a media-centric, full-service digital marketing company that will help Isobar gain further digital media scale in China, as well as get senior Chinese talents in servicing local and international clients," said Jean Lin, Isobar's CEO, Asia-Pacific, in a statement to "Thoughtful China," according to AdAge's Normandy Madden. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3K_rWGRYDam9GK0PMcGjiME1_zRCpu-Fz7DL6ejc_aNSTHS9ALRP-qV1cEzVr2FAX7nQulY3p5JXugChl5It1TETfX_S9FAHpVkz9SuuxHBqDEFZPNaXsUmkvGEZg-eWOPmpHA06uDEeauFZ_kp6Ylquy3sa6_QTk-4muFdqG-zQHbOQYdgCBAaZUqh6hvMk8xQkjS4m1IL67ZiBoX1XUR8PpOFMoTljPzeDiO5tMRIjb5FK9dQsDqocfBgiE_xKd9txe4eec8lBlss_uCdV0otU3BdJKaqumsh8pyfk7nRsrZLk56BNlgBkZJLanAHYgFh4o9QiZ5-H9Npk1JZfDDYzYDO7GBcqPGeBB0Sv1gxhPAIci5Fdrj_-I6SHpqaG5PyzuAN0Kw8yw==> . 


Outbrain Outreach


Marketers realized years ago that the Hispanic community represented the fastest growing consumer segment. And with more ad dollars, comes more content (and vice versa). Content marketing specialist Outbrain is expanding its existing partnership with Univision to help the Spanish-language media company drive up its pageviews. "This extension will generate a new revenue stream that benefits our audience, while meeting the rising interest from our advertisers," said Charlie Echeverry, executive vice president, Interactive Media Sales, Univision Interactive. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00197wlaOnxN3IQUv3MDfiW-ycj4kyYoZAe6x0FwE7igNWsUkT3zUdVDd0hK90MQ1ES-RIQ4BBK3Zs_NUNSpTobe_SgAdo_pNGcfFrYbKCpi_nRTlncv5nasAJBLSn1sbt1_cM4zVBqaKC-CLSz2IQatqwXOd3svuFn3t3EQqCw9kWzHCD8hoyvFLDd-ne1ZZhoIrowOE9yG3sUZQ0EQZbv7XGoFUx6K_YiBYtuNkHJ4Uvn8ybrPD9aJz49B9bTt4L60F-7zNmxiHk=> .

Do Not Track Meltdown


Do Not Track will have to wait for next year. After 14 months of sometimes harsh debate via email, phone and in-person meetings, the Worldwide Web Consortium (W3C) working group charged with creating specs for the browser mechanism has all but ground to a halt. To try and advance the process, the W3C has brought in Peter Swire, a privacy official in the Clinton White House, to mediate between privacy and industry advocates. But even the new guy acknowledges a resolution in 2012 is unlikely. Meanwhile the ad industry may see an opportunity to reinvigorate its self-regulatory program. As IAB general counsel Mike Zaneis tells the New York Times, "We've seen the W3C falter. So industry is redoubling its efforts to come up with a meaningful standard for browser controls." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sjqa2LlVVYAxysxLa7BmyX29bGU9AR1ecI9i_0Xq7i8R4wiE-kelrnv2ZaceKSZXxzcdaecEgiTsNdPXY8_-9Hp44etozBUUog-Mgs9qtflccYw242rPscZ6dgM6oNFXxIgOnggv5d5oFYx1pLAonNKOVvF-KUNzU4xC_d9_KRdoKUjqAxkzTX2lJScpL4H7gV_thSTx4wBow==>  WSJ story (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6shajC5wXNYQ9cpDiuGMGr33-uiaUvTgJdW6ojddwighbqt0NDX-pyeV2vRGI8hGrZLF_hSKcgnoPZBZ12_epgx_7XXl8MXOUymSuUeQbpDmMXxb68NhafebOs6pvLHy6ZU3oWHFUQz-d__VR4JFbA9_FmTvRWoIYcFCG6t33jyReuWlSMC0oADtQfVOlhJafjqLP1duqMdD2nSYuVuebXVl>  


Direct Sales Be Damned


All the cavilling <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sgScBcSDi7CSGviT-YMAWCpMaCc6ffXF62I1Jf0e5UpwqtCvfkUT7nBI_2-rtMlTPNHnx9p3oqxvcRXJnmn0saa4segziwY20ldylRfL8wDLw==>  about online advertising being a cheap, direct response medium comes mostly from those with an "old media" ad bias, argues Triggit's Zach Coelius in an Adweek opinion piece. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6shnCBvLjtUFKBDiQyqB5jNuZoSOb5aCrFsJBP4D0anBb78UKya5KmgQgCLuRNNfH0VjXzEog9LlT7e9eECz9QkOd2lp1rC6umVZZHVSogCkJCYGTzdcs-tduh59IvPxcugUqa2BR7tNBvu4iQ8T7Mq_7Q0bWkpdnI2VPzTKGn7XYw==> . "The automation of the buying process enables advertisers to buy more efficiently at larger scale," Coelius writes. "More of their growing ad budgets can be passed to publishers, rather than being spent shuffling paper." A punch to the agency gut. Time for an AdExchanger "ripple dissolve" from 2011: the fun starts at 30:30 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sha3p4BWHi9nGEdlLNnPtazwCbdZWJ3WJhK4GZys2_Uop0i_J4hjiKrSbhP7nqK0cyuyUIUtGPCGyyL2aJCqX2yeEq6EZZqmCccMfcaDOjt1bWOnbYHhEDNH05TyvuhP_k=> . 


Agile Ad Ops


So many ad tech vendors to sort through, so little time. What's a publisher to do? Mimi Wotring, SVP Strategic Development & Operations for quadrantONE, advises publishers in an AdMonsters post to focus and prioritize. And quickly. "In this new ad tech era, the modus operandi for modern day publishers is to focus your teams on the technological innovations that stand to further your business objectives," she says. "I know it sounds simple, but I am proof that with so much going on, it is easy to get lost in the vacuum of technological innovation with no clear plan, just endless meetings and demos with potential partners." Hoover more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sgLk4D8sgmyuXVZpT_YNlmcKU0C_AJPCW35-yELu21Eyt3g8nzFf7V2X-nvLk3uSCK_R34744efDAO-eZtlNslq9ABWoJybij-Tyyyv9Y0UwHW5Aeru8RdfPy70jvE4DBJUzFSPlGUmEkyWD5oYHsx0fcmXC58GpEJf5eA_H5sqI1K538C-Kcb6> . 


Google Clips Coupon


Google has snapped up Incentive Targeting <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6shcC9LHNM_dqS8-nTCX4kYa0Z2njY6N_Cz6J-jQ9g20CeCMOk4lt678SPOqWxKsbDrA0jAeZ58AQBRAOj4VZKItAmj_5R4-BhGQovD5qeog_cGzauAa77OcInmfssVZ0zA=> , which supports targeted coupon delivery for retailers, in particular grocery chains. As TechCrunch reports, the company has been funded to the tune of $4.4 million and will most likely reside within Google's mobile commerce group. Here's the company's one-liner on itself. "Incentive Targeting sells highly relevant, high value grocery promotional campaigns through a self-service website." More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sjH1FxznoKz5lVbwMO2kGPx0CdK-pnDMyKTy-dXa98H7hs6cD5i0j92_I0aCPs3keV2g-FvdoKh4awCiNSQXVXnYM_80SXsy-VIztOaaCcsOQ68H2YDSxBuVeeyl0wWkaRlV39CQsTVSwBfo6y1yEie0-N2RP4IKXwECygeUuLNGW5HKSniGGyNus3E16M10Hc2ttm8VnBFwj506EvH_JKxIjQk7pEJ7_o=> 


comScore's Impression


In a company blog post, comScore says that a new Media Ratings Council's "take" (see AdExchanger <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sg-xjnXqcEbLevbTY8tpcfHeeNBYnmH-j8JqszlfUCxSvhEiovvh2y1fUuRFWcX_fFykhDcjfGrh0CePHwZXFt-PCPkWvdkI4ymO4kHL-9Wyd_2bUBLAqE3d3Lsp-CbHfcI5tQSeDKRwdpMpfoUuERwKW2I5hlES6UihiIB5BHpOniJIiB8mp5djH8H_w8pGL5AO7a_Y0PZrwbCzhS68UD9> ) on Making Measurement Make Sense (3MS) viewability metrics initiative has holes. Besides itself, comScore identifies viewable measurement study participants Double Verify (sued by comScore <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sijAnIhqsvCXH3EucovGkWsaMiIoHM8buCURlTBg4NskMjOYPR3wFAk_drP11yF_wjn5LFfASraG3Oww7HVra_kvyNvL9Xk60rLZf4oxWLrXANwhNzEfTzKPKZqYil_IB3kx8hWoVMyTv94FrnDy8Lr5duxg1zcpIRdUgswGkUb2w==> ), Google, Moat (sued by comScore <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sijAnIhqsvCXH3EucovGkWsaMiIoHM8buCURlTBg4NskMjOYPR3wFAk_drP11yF_wjn5LFfASraG3Oww7HVra_kvyNvL9Xk60rLZf4oxWLrXANwhNzEfTzKPKZqYil_IB3kx8hWoVMyTv94FrnDy8Lr5duxg1zcpIRdUgswGkUb2w==> ), and RealVu. Anne Hunter, comScore's VP, Advertising Effectiveness Products, says her company is the only one that is accredited to provide metrics for cross-domain iFrames which block some data about viewability. She adds, "While the cross-domain iframe measurement is certainly not the only issue in viewability tracking, it is the most significant significant one." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6siyF93-3yX2obHLIJWg6J-rDYoo0dQuuZ4o8WuHg8mBihrBC0Mnw_6It6OejJLKwYWfXb3GrjT1JbKzVojEoXNWCsPztOpqrGCyW5xOWPqerEJj-GwU6lIU9q4zZatyNaUV6wncR3b1PHqcOQLKVlPYme9uh9OXemlyYO8ctShQ9JqTKzzwH8ZlNwILx7kSQdE=> .

Your Stack, My Algos


On All Things D, the opinions were flying yesterday. Digital enfant terrible and Mediaocean CEO Bill Wise sends a hatchet Google-way seeing mediocrity ahead with Google's tech stack. Wise concludes with a bit of veiled self-interest, "... the marketing community really needs to ask if Google is the best business to provide the end-to-end tech stack that marketers want. For Google's tech stack competitors which don't have ad inventory to sell (Adobe, for example), the chief reason to create a tech stack is to provide marketers with a suite of useful, integrated products, and to make money in the process. That's a setup for a win-win (pending good execution, of course)." Adobe buys Mediaocean - you heard it here first! Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6sjBsU02Xs7Jua-ERo7nJ5ozGt9M7f4bHohZSJwOZi9Y5LQRR-Q44uspfRDo5Ks7cpjDWz3Otb4vBU28x3GiOqiMlKrtPReauIXQDP-mFle1Bi3eisHMrIH47fNSj-n8ROFlr0pdUT78eQd6owBYhCETMAmdFYEfP7z9xkJJSZmOwuuAYjkcHofpU4FlpFeHssQ=>  And, in an unrelated piece, Rocket Fuel CTO Mark Torrance kicks targeting data to the curb: "If I were told I had to either give up all the third-party data I might use, or give up my use of algorithms, I would give up the data in a heartbeat." Poor data. Algo lovers unite. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001dAxfOAXh6siW8ySMpaKumWqwjL_c8KCAGU2A8rAr-6xGrkgIzis_H3QEA5BipmsIhT9kc-f_jwluw2GHAaTx-R6FAgD5p2-SpSRsX71O_kdCTaAtNBs8w4O3ucWhxw2fvLV5BFa2EaQhnYeoiH2X4J_my6tFtlMFc6275oLaBxnUiSGOpQds4aKrM94BU8dS>

Price Per Second


On Digiday, Josh Sternberg takes a look at StumbleUpon advertising and its "native" formatting. He finds a creative pricing structure: "The most common pricing for advertisers on StumbleUpon is a flat fee of 10 cents per engagement of anything five seconds or more (anything less than five seconds, the advertiser doesn't have to pay). For specific product or movie launches, there's a premium of 25 cents per Stumble (the act of going from page to page via StumbleUpon), which gives advertisers increased priority to skip ahead in line." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc-wVYJoJLQ_ZVvn1eS6hh4SMlASyPlImi-H5eZF_a6zydCToOE_ZpW0GgopgW1-pi55FIWfeKiNC2TlMEp5CpS-a0HETZtNzlmClY8FYTs93LsbqgDUE8dRMR7y2kr0Y1T8Jbi7KibuE2kcQ8VehArXsPFy_X37V0imRiGvECAtjQyyJlB5vcgc> . 


Platform Press


Ad trading platform Digilant (née Adnetik) decided it was time to talk "growth story" yesterday. According to a press release, the company saw an "85 percent increase in revenue, a 41 percent increase in staff, and several new innovative products launched over the past 12 months." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc9gM5jbfJ5aOKKJeXATgP0Vh9srM6cIlX1Xdqi0PnFba1zvwjmvBg8MKkKSG-nDWEYlfqGP7__8htsC-1E-LNa_hawWGjmSRc17N9lFoGJKDv2_53MXVyOMIR5CeY6Y_r54R1czJQQW8FdL8gp2GuYdXCT6UqHShKA5jYvvMoJ8ShIcnMw4DA3Y09p--dQdy8f6-DMB1A_8as2sivFWGc6nKffj_o-HnbV9VUAT4j8NePsUKawfo1Md>  


Matching Pixels


Data exchange and platform BlueKai and mobile ad network Jumptap are claiming a first-of-its-kind innovation. From the release, "Jumptap is expanding its data offering by more than 14,000 data segments via combined Jumptap and BlueKai data partners. Segments include consumer purchase intent, past purchases, geographic and demographic data, interests, lifestyle, and automotive, among others." Read more - including how pixels are matched to mobile audience <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc89_sRzLghjVTIQH2kmwcwav5ob8yOv0NcvrZys1nsCz0cfhZL8z1K-BO3x81i3zFwlHrhIk-pz6dLF4Lw_SFxGEUvIMlDRMVyMVFfCc5HpKawiYXdxmmCCW0y6hlkWQs4RBMd0a6emleG0Z9_PYV0thOntCJzkzcc1STZmdem2a5MqoQa5Gdit1RvCLRCiaYSER9LlLhvEGVtZXpXbk__fv3bbXXZcb8c=> . 


Mobile RTB To-Go


A Y-Combinator startup, LeanMarket (see the site) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc91hZ9k-Tq3TLc1auMswpQoS0TAjjSjuXZTVugmf0cOY-oXSAL4oka49nC_7V3iFN8bwcN4KV7eQKdefEPBNCuBZAr1r6990AM=> , is positioning as a real-time bidding (RTB) buying platform for mobile according to Venture Beat. Where's the differentiation? The article says it has to do with transparency: "Advertisers can see exactly which apps their ads appear in and can monitoring their activity through real-time reports." Also, the company says no minimums and no contracts. Just step up and buy some. You decide. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc8c_DI-5GAtGRn19mcwHqLBujv-suYsZnI0fixZaGLrxsTo7EzepzKS4owEIzZoe9Ehum5yxsCOsfd9Mt-CxzQsmNwgVcJptkNLU2Ez7vsD-IULUNJzy6ZWceQzGjTi9LiLEoivglhsQFtZ_m7KxBEdy4CLhr8utWFe48dcstEQXilqRyUxK5nfFpXHjVi2VTDiw-Vg4DZYiKOIk4yM-hqk7sqvbXz9rmjfs_A8DQpLzpJxTc_rzaT8>  


UC's Cookie Census


Not surprisingly for privacy researchers at University of California (UC) Berkeley, each cookie count yields more cookies (or "trackers"!) than the last. Their latest tally shows a 23% increase in the number of third-party cookies dropped over six months. The most prevalent third party cookie dropper is a certain DMP. As AdAge notes, "BlueKai set the most cookies on the top 100 sites in October -- 328 up from 321 in May... Bluekai also set the most cookies among the most popular 1,000 sites. However, in that category the number of cookies it dropped fell from 2,906 on May 17 to 2,562 on October 24." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc-_ebAOs7B-q3AB3UwodLYId1uJbPuJ5AoqhmQkoA8DVK_WTdUeScsXmV56um_v1f6ZdSiRzbEYt1lO5J3VZafX-BCV7xmpeF--VDhG1kc3OPpcSuOYEBd_rbxrnYY7eYh14WHU3_XA_pe2SF8mJzGHlFV5h-cci39CL0ThfU7r-OXUvhXhXoxVmJRUQMSw6Mw_KobN7l8kWkUklFSraWhv>

Cyber Monday = Black Friday


Akamai, the content delivery specialist, looked at traffic patterns for e-commerce on an hourly basis between Black Friday and its online version, Cyber Monday (a day largely spent at desks and computers, not malls). There wasn't that much difference in activity. "The only clear difference is that consumers chose sleep over shopping as illustrated by the 25% decrease in browsing activities at 12AM," said Akamai's senior program marketing specialist Elyssa Duboys in a blog post. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc8DFbsWJXJYDF4K57z3_-PfxMhfvEAGz1w7-dDhGMGxIRqDITW9FuTx_TlTvwfVnIk1fwRIvGppcU67TeRmq1MP-qJPan6b1vyXnO531bdkUf6iZn8colbVogRI51BXcTNOz9vhwsVGqCPoSyiRCLD1caJ8G5A6t6yCrTTbSnWV4uj3Wpczd4Z2a4weLLiarlq563JUSrRb1Q==> . 


Big Data Dance


On The Makegood, publishers' biggest decision is to figure out who to bring to the consumer data "party" says Shelley Eleby, quadrantOne's director of marketing and product strategy. After that, Eleby adds, "Just Dance. This is an opportunity to learn. This is not a point in time solution but an ongoing strategy that will continue to refine and 're-imagine' itself as technological innovations advance, as users become more educated about the digital data trail they leave, and as..." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc-0CtPfpDHYlzG4EE6zQEklUs3gxjfsaB8n_4qeutFV7iomry2XorXZJvypjEoG21cwHtuyMl57ll4QsxVbh89cL1Pp_PDwN4wE2b0SsCcnAxlRi4GHQ0FNt8Qt-v4WoJEiA5EuvyPXHRhqj9LN6eTF93PMWui0DH84Q6zs6kHXuCnZgef1JfyhhGe1PT-zWxkV-XhMVwam4sFLWfeTLrIz> . 


RTB 'Flash Crashes'


Similarities between ad exchanges and financial exchanges may extend to their vulnerabilities, Jasper Jackson argues in a column on The Media Briefing. He looks at phenomena associated with High Frequency Trading (HFT) such as "Red Queen syndrome" and "flash crashes." (Oh, the imagery!) The stakes could be high for real-time bidding (RTB), Jackson writes. "HFT peaked in 2009, when it accounted for 61 percent of all US stock trades. It has since fallen back to 51 percent - and profits from HFT have fallen to a quarter of their 2009 levels." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013KpkbEg2Rc9acVAVWiQ3CmVNV6pcE04dlDF_ynOT4UPpigM0qRN6O0l7BFraDyPR4aEI6mBAWQ64Viqhg4zsN6nv4pYB0koCiWmidCx_RtBa47FynV9B8spY1M-yFAg5C8H05JIr_erytfXxZ3YdWAQ9Nxc1PHS4YX_CFaqomATgxQ_s87L7ZFTkC1fU_7sl8IJSSO7oHeE=>

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>

Upfront Momentum? 

This past spring's attempt to formalize <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU3YIHa7VxPrS31H5lNepUp5MLiIdCuEl48D2Cn7MlWNyCabQbxRt95QC5dlUBTVJRJef3nOXW4ebAi30bpeZEci_NQqWJIL3QFDA5NAihCLnamsr3XuLmtJpT9ZOm4PoyjiwPR4GhYPeyBV7gRVtrK6pKgAOoePw2MbL_GKuE3TepJSwiSNVB6BsKvZb9rs37pHvRYpUTR8x599tQYAElVD9NB9y1e-TNOkkkRd-2ecsA==>  Digitas' NewFront -- the four-year-old online ad sales-focused event designed to capture the attention of media buyers attending the TV upfront presentations -- was a big production. And now, the Interactive Advertising Bureau says it will produce the show. "The impression that it was owned by a single agency looked like it would impede future growth," IAB CEO Randall Rothenberg told the NYT's Tanzina Vega. "They wanted the optics to be much more inclusive of the broader digital ecosystem." Read the NYT's report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU2ZVTwdp3O3I-oE5Hs2enMUpuvZdP9o3LnqHBoGbG0DqwrzWdkhhOu84Q1XsN8hKHsS8rlq2TrGwVt0s9kNIRvDT-q0snhDNL7CnCDrYSM2LBJVsCD2m36rQ-RBAMbvPvlxgati13skYt98AubwvkrqtVO3R1UA0sBvumM5GCWX8sEq3lcByb9jBKNqKoxcWCthkdJmmWs08w==>  or check out the IAB release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU2IyOOQKrgBvUctXP-CorcdDuWsQ-T4oTgLz4NFoESdwg6e44ezkTeTKRnvHs2MBOOGOMc-rzch5XyJDMHhaSRaH7mFduZJVRzBvJ_6bokL1sBAKZc4-xxAA3LEjvP34EFY7GgOLSlR-D1QO7KgTY3AXaWyySoAr38DpO6ox-nO_Q7Sx0PXO6v_fV2Iafx4CTBnLpXpfx1gkMfDhdNNXqsz> . 

FBX Price Premium 

Bernstein Research analyst Carlos Kirjner believes Facebook Exchange will offset price pressure on Facebook's traditional ad revenue, as noted by AllThingsD's Peter Kafka. "If the Exchange wasn't around, [Kirjner] says, conventional ad pricing would drop 5 percent next year, and 5 percent the year after that. But after factoring in the growth of Facebook Exchange, which adds a big pricing premium, Kirjner figures those ads will remain flat next year, and drop a bit in 2014." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU0Th-OFpu_5zsA0fbrjRUgpV0GmLzbvJiRM5u-_KgLUgMZsAuBA02_SErX8oShda6P8pXJV_OlLqtKcSdP3vu2fsWSfFyLqRIvoL9-dNHn1rl2-DNIQWLhQth8qwKpb4RJPAUbw0MSX_c0c1sqKUnBc4S_izsSllOSFg5F_yl3ErgWOFHRz1c3eheRRg_AiOKSug89RCuQvEcyTVRD_6sdW> 

Real Tryptophan Bidding 

By its nature, RTB volume rises and falls with consumer internet traffic. In the case of Thanksgiving, that means a big fall-off in bid volume as Americans unplug to spend QT with loved ones. Mediapost covers Accordant Media data finding "average daily trading volume for RTB impressions fell between 10% and 30% during Thanksgiving week vs. corresponding market averages." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU14ld5OPK6K2-ekhzTXCmB2t43R9NDe4AJPEFY1lZzO10Lv7gL_mp4tjd617FPCeDmuCoPBL5FOy-oUfUQDRRTCqSBN6DR50rfjxDtKs-kXQXeD5mdI9ahyoE_aPbwT5B-8VrGwPaED_ytAlT4pOdRNT2imNmW35KY1bDafqW0nrZQbB9sZY-J-gHOjIw9qTTylp8i9HH31n9BQCIry3r3xHRjovRUK3Q4=>  

Federated Media's Growing Pains 

"Conversational marketing" specialist Federated Media has the online ad industry talking about it a lot lately, and not all of it is positive. The company, which recently said it would shift away <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU20Tx5rCZQvdLHO9t81THIdTKB7koFfodY0XRmqqobamMZIJGehLGbC_gH0xfewmZBTXJ49OoKxvPzBpY7oiDxPihotN-E4ruFK2TB2zsf71iy1T8pra-CtTTjPiRY7uPw21-YDUs6-F0UxfYEArH9Ero-F_8c8vA9KCbGzTDBM7B8UbfxXcYBggOq1XSwJIGS6WzcATpe046VKN6RvrlhlFCHj_dd0Piw=>  a bit from direct sales in favor of its programmatic tools through its Lijit unit, is the subject of a long post-mortem by Business Insider's Alyson Shontell, who discusses the grousing about CEO changes and challenges presented by rival upstarts like Say Media, which has embraced FM's old direct sales model wholeheartedly. "Say took FM's model and did it the right way," an otherwise unidentified ex-FM staffer says. "It's the company FM should have been." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU1tE3g0ZFgUIqSWcih_DfZVAtXUR5FjVN6Lds2zHFAvuEusHuE7omM9cFPHlEADrNU6D_kC1VWSXrmwQKkB0ntY8aPlsrxGvNgYbODDZJUbat2qorC1RbloqMY4BsyOL2OAp7n4rfUMdQeruHQuhQadPuGlzu7j9IGZNCTruEZB3w==> . Related: read about the death of the banner <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU1HMmo0AeuFvHHj1vjeQVHOoryZ3HNlhEZsGekluyUpzKT8HwAyWZZZ6OlSGJbUEA4dztK9d2GzMBExAyZ2f2ejGfAn-w7kjUpDmQeFbrRgTWVpYYCPlvshDtU7es67H2HL62gc0KKq5MKj9nNK4PZycd_Mao1tA9s=>  (again). 

Do Niches Need Data? 

Well, who doesn't need data these days? Jeff Roberts, writing in paidContent, concludes that niche publishers, who by their very nature don't attract a varied audience, can probably continue to go without the use of private exchanges and the like. As one unnamed New York publisher told Roberts, "While we are a BlueKai customer, our experience is that most advertisers do not require audience segmentation data as part of their buy... My guess is that it's probably more important for publishers with a more mass audience. Our audience is relatively targeted (and valuable) already and so segmentation isn't needed to get the audience advertisers are seeking." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yOko5e0-KU1zx_s_dxdUK2-He6eaki93sHPP7UPV6PUq3BwcPmXxlzCiN6cUly8X0mvwibG9uYyrrl1jEAkW5SQvxC02skv_Xmk0KnOYExjMnAJQkM1Zm7UR3tDNtoquV1AMUGbJNhNmG12T6Mv8MmO5JCZ0B87sKNmII1JkkD_gqxSQauzFNEowxN23U23QTz-9C4N2Z5vg8t17EdoJNWs9KJnipMnC> .

Chango And Cash


Chango, the self-described, programmatic marketing platform has raised $12 million to help build out its retargeting system. In addition to ramping up its technology, the company is looking to hire at least 50 new engineers and sales people. "Our clients are among the most progressive advertisers and agencies in online retail and we're achieving a 90% renewal rate," claims Chris Sukornyk, Chango's founder & CEO. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEzlZ3gCI-iAtTCBh3xNy_JOKEOM2NldwTNY2fXZCb_SSWBauff8unykeWerDFZRA32sNZ0d1ZD-jVEfhQQHrwlXhu3C9Oi6wLaUfnK6Sn0YhDY7-gh5s56fYphzfhALPjmlh_xfugZCSiZ0K2QrUp1U> . 


Facebook Ad Choices


Ad Age's Jason Del Rey covers Facebook's decision to not use the Ad Choices icon favored by the Digital Advertising Alliance on its site's ads. Del Rey explains, "Users can generally opt out through the DAA's icon in two or three steps, but on Facebook, they might need to take at least four actions to opt out of behavioral targeting." Retargeted ads through Facebook Exchange also come under scrutiny. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hExHg0evC6cA1Z5Eou1OWwpX0kQDKzfCMaZkwcqKBNCBDbmBc4njF18kWOvXctGM90X2uzuxQ6QD51LaKkiNX1x6Bb4XiaouTqBtn1OLp6gO5mvWWbj3Vg0hnuwkomMa-6jlHdqmSFHOS7ht762XmmOLBmwL-_V52r8oR1OfMm6w19_asljjS3B3TMCjTgmFMakaTXFDasPF6Q==>  


Real-Time 'Showrooming'


It's a real-time war when it comes to the battle between brick-and-mortar retailers and their online competitors. The WSJ details some of the showrooming <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEwqmGygiMgvh_nXg5SLcwq1B-bUc0vuxxHTkuwFtTIY7jLJoQWzIXxiKfKmch87Fz8tjkMIGg--01Oyv9G36Z-GlTq_AFtfosbFWU4dKBeAsg-8rvs0uhkt5IoCCECUzSaZCbJGjTfyhmWZ3X1XvyBkFZ9N6ofYLyA=> -related shenanigans over the past week, "When Target advertised plans to sell a $400 Dyson Ball vacuum cleaner for $269, Best Buy responded by cutting its online price for the vacuum by $80, to $300. Best Buy wasn't immune. When the electronics retailer published a circular advertising it would sell a $1,500 Nikon camera for $1,000, Amazon.com followed up Thanksgiving morning by cutting its price for the same camera to $997." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEzu_MUfLh8QKz0U-F6jZqTPYsmKE4XqMc43V_vzyld3BvPNEgE54_x_4y3TCK3G31DUr8tnxfoEuE0Xo3Knltpk0K3Q7n1JTJKzFXjf2tKbo0UQwXkGX7gfQg6rhrwdt2i36FzZAuGZmocfGxYjljhcFixYQD6kKR-PfZ_g6gOfZwxjIc8TpBXf> . Imagine all that data hooked up to a retargeting campaign. A big data mess. 


Bad Views


Marco Bertozzi, executive managing Director, EMEA, at Publicis' Vivaki Nerve Center, is one who takes a dim view of the viewable impressions quest. "Viewability is a classic example where we are setting a bar so high vs the other the channels because we can...I would ask that we take some time to establish some very clear guidelines and transitions and not go in like a bull in a china shop just so we can show off at the next pitch. Lets do things right, for the good of the industry, not just the next sell," he writes on his personal blog. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEzoOfceHNfflUlysexugXgBC7bVmLEiz9D1SMeoWoO4BgSaWY8z_0JzO178LhU_AR21a7aSl62RIgi6-n--snsYIe-Ww0KfBOI4f1SNdpsQ14llTkQkxe4kwKhk3l2P3Q2x0we-NzwxFDW9ar6uthXJ3SWzYt30pNOrJG52uuUi8Oq2iLYMcg4re0JqWoyTTolBwYs6VhKbLClQRxuYXj4A> . 


NSFW, But Safe For Ads


"Adult ad network" ExoClick is boasting that it has reached an "all-time traffic record" to hit more than 2 billion ad impressions a day on both web and mobile devices. The company doesn't divulge what that means in terms of actual dollars, but nevertheless, it's bragging that it's the biggest adult ad network (as opposed to... ?). ""We are very proud of this new record and it's only thanks to our talented team and all the clients that trust in our company," says CEO Benjamin Fonzé. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEyvILX1ps3qR20PFPND-U1Us2T7GofqnvjZut3tqBWiqOEDHO6LkD87q00dLKv0UexteeTXcbgDsiW7qtG-dmenJaf4LSNG3sQUVefN4rAahiDXPWE3zqXZNQJT2qZ2t28Z-DALnzw2ii3qwh2jgYtzmZrfRvT2vXY971tn7Z8xjM2mmH7UsYkSsT4ZryIrHLk=> .

Wilson Slaps Programmatic


Venture guy Fred Wilson writes about the sudden absence of ads on his popular AVC blog, and explains the reason is Federated Media's decision to get out of direct sold premium ads altogether (AdExchanger story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hExtfEzhMJHgT9oiw9MIgT-_u8mUVaSMkhg3aqG20ozf8XTz1PXhAuZSW9-36_HEj6atpr3x_5AyqZ9XbAEkFLUUobNIpnjw8dXUG8QJA2WXQrEte7AgtPGp6skP-rtsq9R5zM4XEoRRKge-WkdXUYh3EwXT0L0q6fn4bb8KsPQ7fRSXH8_ihsvQSuwd9yEWtE8hrq0kXbuJh1CvnSBrNpPWkiLKwT9Gjdk=> ) and go all-in with its Lijit programmatic ad platform. Wilson says, "I could keep running the programmatic ad units that have been on display here as of late, but I find that uninteresting to me and likely to all of you too. Instead, I want to explore more conversational marketing oriented (ie native) advertising here on AVC." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEySiF0tXuiBzrXbRkHApokG7QzqshWh-OC0fmamuzh3BNX6QnGzMP81rWvyIkF1MSqsp9MkY0tdvI8wyr10ql-Nj6AnnKnlg1enkcv7K-f9qovGF477ugjcHfv5iSv8kgTCD8EPAH5TZdlgenSaYJzre-n7_D5TNCk=>  


Foursquare Pushback


We're hearing more tales fundraising turbulence, as companies struggle to get new rounds at high valuations. The latest story is on Foursquare, which the Wall Street Journal reports is expected to take just $2 million in revenue this year. Not only that, monthly users are apparently 8 million, despite 25 million registrations. "Potential investors aren't convinced the company is moving quickly enough to make money and are concerned that the use of its free service...is starting to slow, the people said." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001WZi5I576hEyHTCPObSNly00MDWIYJ_ODIwoEy_tOwYIevcVBhkDhuceHnrZs_KmCWp-VFw6BvVOi2wEGpHizeuLJnAsRnmbL499UejkNX1_HRpGYrGRA_E5l7xO3OygNlh6fR2iQl2XOBl8KQcbO-nWQUcDoslzNRGFbwTBXu8o2MLE1eBJge5jpGg8UsdYp>

Do Not Track Unboxed


AdAge takes Microsoft's Internet Explorer 10 browser for a spin to see how the default Do Not Track setting works. Ad Age's Kate Kaye writes, "The DNT tool can't be found under the Privacy settings where many users are bound to look for it. Rather, it's buried within the browser's Advanced settings, where a check box is automatically checked to 'Always send Do Not Track header.'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012FT3vV84q6CM0jhDweDVuOofk0uekFn52PpsVCE5DRMBJqtku0Bfj2U6hwjIJhlgXOQKHQRVfVZQRLVxK6qAv20xyfuGKjoea-nchL-rUht7r1v_677VJJSeW_zpRxR5jYVem_HM2yD1iXdmZLMZiWyHlHcZtYpvTKyuJTE6Dy6QkOh9RoEDUg==>  


IPG Quits Facebook (Investing)


Interpublic Group has sold the remainder of its shares in Facebook, acquired in 2006 for apprximately $5 million. Reuters points out, "Shares of Facebook, which debuted with a market value of more than $100 billion in May, have lost nearly half their value since then on concerns about money-making prospects." A little more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012FT3vV84q6C2eXw1tzMQTQvhzbXPHpsonS4O-h1CB5W9TOygYdS8F90-AtHrak9SQm6pdO82I2hIDbngFpUXPWvHihqniUa4QICz188JwOcKqYSQANFU62mrC17EPdtM78NzSz_BBtbnVsoP63iiPhPeN2Db92Y47rCeQ56tmXNNOFtD4GcijwvK3_eyq3_Fg1gPfNmrbUXtuwuzDOUccDIyVfTu25Mo>  


Yahoo's TV Guide Play?


Every since Marissa Mayer took the Yahoo CEO seat this summer, speculation has been rampant about what sort of acquisitions she might make. The rumor mill has swirled around a number of companies in the programmatic space, but so far, nothing. In place of that, eyes are now on -- of all things -- TVGuide.com, the digital version of the "what's on primetime?" listings publisher. According to AllThingsD's Kara Swisher, "Yahoo is only kicking the tires to determine if the site would add to its online media efforts and that such a deal is not in a final state." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012FT3vV84q6BUXjfJouVmZ82lJoouM8F5bhIfmqL_NXy1tD1AuGjrjGpDhgt8sNTMxpg5LeSTrQl071_pUS6CQBApCk0IDWbkPH3D5_2h56Yn2Y9JxaHjGGRxz_lNpHe09Elz_cXsPA0cYMZkKScvclHsS45Iow8z7Oq_yQvxRgcZjT-MWaxVzX8TxN2OWXKNCbHm6Yd4vmvL5g2qLVjiwjt3D101AKqP> . 


Flip This Tablet


Video ad network YuMe is rushing to keep up with the pace of different tablet products -- and the growing amount of video viewing being offered on these quasi-portable devices -- by releasing a few new ad units designed to provide additional support to cross-platform sales. Among the new ad units is the Mobile Flip, which YuMe says helped extend the CW's primetime TV ads to tablets during the fall season. "Using our SDK and the YuMe Ads Framework, for the first time, brands can deliver unique tablet video branding experiences with a rich and unprecedented variety of interactive, custom executions," says Ed Haslam, SVP of marketing. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012FT3vV84q6BSRuoUhxsfXRIGGNtHEE8dptnBF62Mdy_k9z_-qOY0qzbLIvNcmmcos4-Trk0YC3_DztXm03_jbS4CjKwutY7BLp1b6sqWyo-nWS-m-eAa4L5Pu-egLXVW4CYMuy28V4meWtojmVPkNzoaOFWd3DHfI7zErb4HMjJyFev2eJEG0RmpdorVKP48jxJaayr5oMWZZRxJD0S8bCWhWqfzsvwCJFZLSLgpTNiKVFroFD3fKg==> . YuMe fights the standardization maelstrom in video. A network of proprietary ad formats with scale can be extremely valuable. 


Waiting For Mobile


A panel at the Guardian Mobile Business Summit would appear to be a good moment for cheerleading the mobile ad space, but execs representing WPP's MediaCom and Google mostly just lamented the usual problems associated with driving mobile ads, namely measurement. Ian Carrington, director of Google's mobile and social ad sales, had another reason for mobile's fitful progress: mobile wap sites pretty much suck. "The reason why people don't have good mobile sites is often because the CEO, CMO or IT director doesn't really believe in mobile yet," he said. "Maybe they got their fingers burnt 10 years ago." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012FT3vV84q6DPy2xeYHADVO6fIsUqjGxfr8fdBRmrO8JlDNN8VNEX8ClkIKIoTkf1N77YHPMxC_y1__aCkZiLmtPGpms4wUPO41nz7vLUb6oWjyINCUIPmqPk9ds0hmiXGopZDjTGfo54EdjfK8ZFHjQi0hkRb8QkyUeqC3U5sHxPea31hgs2OhUXn9JNY3ewx9i5vhuZXsJKBANDsdOuIQ==> .

Post-Impression Facebook


TechCrunch's John Constine says that "View Tags" is the new conversion tracking tech used by Facebook that looks at the "viewthrough" conversion - and not just the click. (Read about the new FB conversion pixel on AdExchanger here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012FT3vV84q6C2J7Y76irnF4ZTZYJMMcOqodtfkHgrLAk9O742UkXqDpFj5h3l88L8UM0R6L6OsvKv23DBYG3pw-96JdtlNxjHOaiVdCGuBvFmjtDzsUb_EUzE4qSUbNDyHe5QxWIAbZhi6nMaZqAbdN9W5vKCdJ90_H7PasWPO9bra2fSMatUM07RBoKSyD4-CsBREkJYM7E=> ). He says Facebook Ad API partner "SocialCode ran an ad campaign for a consumer packaged good company looking to get people to redeem an offer. Weather Change


As it continues to ramp up technology aimed at better performance for predicting weather and related ad trends <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DIMbuOxH1cKBvxSL3LSAj0ZEqnpFP3ANGhd_YtWdULaomkSkNcczOg20QZU6jO2Dfd3OOW98_krdRjeOOTc09Az8IbFNXzHdPVToTure_w-GN4jwrhlcnWPbY5m1nvnmVvy33Q8gk7ciX1TbVYx_oYTbrYrVpAKkGRKPm-GlQsoEgFXwyjDPLOr9RLo7lVjyvI8zcDnBJTAmBahaUOaWOvenbHqrBe4hoUepLHsKvqFh4piM7p484X2lT19DPjYh> , The Weather Company (FKA, The Weather Channel) is bringing in ad techj vet Vikram Somaya from Thomson Reuters to run a newly created division called WeatherFX. The new unit will create products around targeting ads to specific neighborhoods and locations and alter what those ads say as weather conditions change. "The only other dataset in the industry that I think compares (to Thomson Reuters) has been Weather's dataset, mainly because I think it's universally applicable," Somaya tells AdAge's Jason Del Rey. "Weather always has some impact; it's just where to prioritize." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DIMbuOxH1cI6ez8Mruj8u1q10MOfNoeKcPhBmOw9gC91dUDgy_3WnmYg0eLjyhCtrqFAZmu7KSdAG_tQBomErBYJ7D3Ec1ZGwpC0hccfj_YC-L-9vEitRWwywKrrxZRtC_rDuRfyfz2VrYS2GFfq3yr0p9UKI9rEmPPqTInOPwfTJxeP6w3t8YcVzrl2C2EV7ayf3Bg4nf-waf3i3dGjR6ExjhZDk6P3lgv1vfpqQIs=> . 


Get Glassy


Project Glass, Google's augmented reality smart glasses product, "is the ultimate expression of the wearable tech trend," says Paul Armstrong of @TheMediaIsDying. And while many media observers may not get what Google is driving at, Armstrong, writing in GigaOm believes that it portends deep changes for media companies. "The eye-tracking capabilities Google Glass poses should make not only media agencies and advertisers salivate but editorial departments as well," Armstrong says. "Shouldn't better measurement, placement, contextualization, optimization of editorial (not to mention ads) be what we're all fighting for? Now we might have something that can do it! What's the holdup?" Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DIMbuOxH1cJSd1tzS5iRXFdKG58t8MQS4leJyU1pYpm-wfVLVSGck7fPZJTUxBCYXpnhVJ7R5ypL7r4JLSAVsNMLtImrtP6KofRYcJVMBxWsWBoiVWc-gpq-Xgl12bE72ovEj7iEAtdHNWa0MfCZsaWU0l4jaBG3ZaDkg1Bt-4HGt2RA-aBNzze3Yr5Tkub-XPo2BZOdjedDJT3VFBNwFik2wQd9TxAVGHvo4mrypmBoTWoN1GHUxw==> . 


Social TV Consolidation


While the consolidation wave and implosions haven't actually materialized (yet) in social TV/entertainment, social entertainment check-in pioneer GetGlue has agreed to be acquired by newer rival Viggle for $45 million in cash plus stock. "With this deal, we are combining very experienced and creative product, engineering and management teams that will continue to build great user experiences and provide industry leading platforms for consumers, networks and advertisers," Viggle CEO Robert F.X. Sillerman said. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DIMbuOxH1cI1zzkp0RBQ8ZNA2azdsBfMKorTyY49fERJP3WPTy4RJCa02HLFyyBgEOLjlXYtdjiYcWssPV3ZabuarU4MeeSMadrd4j-V5fKqj0uXFu2pYMrqTTTt0yFP4yqu25sGOanpAhcz_HbEiaaW5Jlcj5Is9HbO_leUEP54yh--Xyl1jnyURIO5aXLQ> . 


Hands off my Google


Two Silicon Valley Congresswomen are warning the FTC to tread carefully in its Google antitrust investigation. AllThingsD describes a letter the legislators wrote in response to leaks suggesting the agency may ramp up its power to demonstrate "unfair competition" by Google. Liz Gannes writes, "Part of this battle is how it plays out in public. If people start thinking of the Google antitrust case as an effort by the government to hurt a shining star of job creation and innovation, that plays a lot differently than a big bad monopolist going after its competition." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DIMbuOxH1cLJnRcV2ZOWp5imkw4qZOXqpkROziHREYXmmPngoF9xb0YGHWzNxHhTPdkMLd6jrrQ02ZemXvLcuxMKMmYNXucnC3xLI2QC3fEVE5j_ToEo_ADI-fI9vubFpPQqz_uHQtPQcWlz4B_7MTelXkBNLlDI5kdZpeXsp-d_9siQ62B2ejV1vVD1fNnB>  


Bamberger to AOL


After a short run as the head of MEC's digital efforts in North America, Jack Bamberger (AdExchanger Q&A) is heading to AOL. He'll be AOL's first head of agency and industry relations, among other things helping bang the drum of AOL's premium display ad platform. He's replaced at MEC by Susan Schiekofer, who joined in 2010 to lead the AT&T digital account. She was previously MD at Neo@Ogilvy. Andy Wasef also joins the agency's N.A. division as head of innovation and technology. MEC press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001DIMbuOxH1cLR0qlEKOPiG8e5BnEcbDu9-V0piGTD_N_DS63dJ-b-pqjs0zo-Lhf-xN3nUzG6TFgF-apZ0otX7MJUDQpBzQMASwTyxWh14y-LDzIFI6Anm7UjtUESjC_UihhY-kHFnZfUx2w19PS8goYyg-IpMh8w67bh9GEqRAl3yb-NI3i5bKNAEwjgKE0-3FE7KqKRVfg=>

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>  

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W0UAqhV0TPO21x4dhIHQgyvAUo3GYmhJNerdNjY1sq7ZXIIQrktHSxlMN9x7nolIFbOcNFbNIv4VTPbMBxtOkXO7T9DTxGMkV54TxFlVJzS25zDgjXuv-97F8HoJAHhmb4=> .

 

Marketing Algos & Real-Time


The New York Times' Tanzina Vega covers digital audience buying momentum and its effect on big publishers. She writes, "That shift is punishing traditional online publishers, like newspaper, broadcast and magazine sites, who are receiving a much lower percentage of ad dollars as marketers use programmatic buying across a much broader canvas." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W2k__0-2Vgn1_wZZjhRl64_rS2oYRM6JFu2D-L8Av56JjQesP0cuzLLneom6EdFowbBtdrnzGTp1NNZMUrdlhWeoTIHXSkDffbbIi1OqtCvJTj3NeaL8rxEeVC46eGmqJTuuk_qGpJD8yec2jxDl_0e6tAQPo4cdIrxlsJv7fvZaNKmcC8plbn39xjJ8G4bciD0rZU4VJZvzMl3CDZXjMk-S5ifZ3sJU9f-t-mf5KFnEQ==> . Meanwhile, the NYT's Natasha Singer looks at the instantaneous side of audience buying, "Ever wonder why that same ad for a car or a couch keeps popping up on your screen? Nearly always, the answer is real-time bidding, an electronic trading system..." Read that one, too. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W1rwCcqs3z4UJH2HW6vn4_3KeG9nW5CLv_gTTO1vvD0aCBhftl7V9fyKlHGJnyeAeccu3kCFydw3tUUZsl58uXVPTTymk55c6-FbxS0MtMutzXQ1qnC1uBr9hDj6HbCqVUSCYiEmsPxK3I-g4D3fErqWhAhMHpLiDl9t3PY2pdAn6XwHAAt1RgxvJo-LRdRWLmyoN1c0OZu-kjFri-Rl81Vlu77FNC6VQY=> 


Big, New Ad Thing


On The Business Insider, Nicholas Carlson cobbles together sources who say that a big Facebook ad product - in partnership with Datalogix - is on the way that could "kill" a "flagship" Yahoo! ad product. Carlson writes, "Our source says this new Facebook product 'closes the loop' on brand advertising in a way that no site besides Facebook is able. This source gave three reasons Facebook can do this and no one else, including Yahoo, can: Scale, scale, and scale." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W2uVYxYhY3RJCijy8yw57541Y-f8KvdQ71A2YRCuxp0ZDjgs5EL1SAyYgtV3aGK6NVXDu9h1DdCW-4G7iaCb-LwYYmLi5hf5NEIiffCtVtjyOg-qRCj23RX674Rth0pD2d9ZoHkfMJZ2JGG4uVThIIC7CRtZ4zdkgKI_fiHoKj6OHohccmJlX17Crn0TcioUk5JWck0QjtlVz3Hbqh6TJQWXUeMlWh5lYo=> . But, hold on a second! Late Sunday, UK's Telegraph reports that Yahoo and Facebook may partner such that Yahoo's search relationship with Microsoft may be annulled. Read about it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W1nrGAuj4qGfJJdIFsj_WNnhe3nijePbW3Vs4RnYirCLL90ziarmq3ildkmfe2t-TEYDpfxoMwqxYu3UyZu7F9MrfRzq3tQh9oI0TTFl3nSYowoLdTx9CNkJPJbEkT7h-XqML1vNlsqk5hfVwATw9HWXm8z3diOu7oEf_crnELGwgJxdt4vrmtp9V2u0YeSaN5xk6ZaL8YNp6JeQhmzltN4za36L6EpKtUrK1veux64tmUmtnBqijAZaxCELS_Iff68P_B5W_zMMg==> . What a tangled web ad technology weaves. 



Tracking Trouble


This could be a case of the right hand not knowing what the left hand is doing with tracking cookies. Following a message from Consumer Reports President Jim Guest imploring subscribers to take up arms against behavioral targeting mechanisms, AdAge's Kate Kaye did some digging and found that the site has tags from at least 10 third-party trackers. Consumer Reports had no immediate comment. "It's time to stop the unwanted tracking once and for all!" Guest's message said, seemingly unaware that such activity was happening so close to home. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W39B20faz4b2XpSWzveDZbkqdAzJHiwTnxQ3U5IR7hw3wyJKuHroMIkUMtUpf1AAG59zn60Ygd-CMvgu1OaBdb2_m4W_0gOLqMc15zPDh-EaaXRP0sv1fPJ95_cSI23bUBbu5wp4rsf_dAiMfGRHe9WbcZlNI8jrGsxbZyJ5Sky5a_wrRymKNtf>  


You Crazy Gamer


Google has games. And Ingress, a new free mobile app and alternate reality game for Android, may turn heads. Naturally, there is an ad component as Ingress will feature offline retailers and products from marketers such as Zipcar and Jamba Juice. "This grew out of us thinking about notions of ubiquitous computing," Hanke told AllThingsD's Liz Gannes. "The device melts away." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W3xKye2QKf7evrEAkYKFwXM_TF4t24sU-xSqNoSf2T7FkXdeN5YXhBUeXYjm2FLHwOLIUj5FSD3M4_BjiZtEHXESvv4L5iwGlLjDGGAELcGLvOOGpeHbRrLK4O3rkKPOUnuht0TcyXfiidqlk_nCiuxu9xqu-KgI-rZbDM97PWlEHVVE0b4y4L3wL9QpijSmuD7nKCjMkZMAA==> . 


Cracking The Purple Whip


All Things D's Kara Swisher reports that CEO Marissa Mayer is doing away with Yahoo!'s long-held tradition of taking a company-wide holiday between Christmas and New Years'. Swisher also notes "there will be new measurements of performance instituted, based on a variety of benchmarks and evaluations, in order to better understand who the best employees at Yahoo are." And, who aren't. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001FX7WvdvS8W1T5hmMyTJC-TCro3VHyy4vwKOH6L-_1fjtSjBtKGSrU_FXYNPr6563lz-y_RrYCJ4yXnsqPzoXXPkemGActMhCXySF6pk-fOT3XR39QoQM1Y-pdUZbol228MuAyz3SeZFB-HwZ9RX7G83Lc1H-VvMoKlUqvfY_DKVjdRmWcQC8OT2LYLceEvdIV9o-KkpTRKDzl9bKU6wOebSwPdiaqzq9AoeHv7nCBytKuO9oqJetIJYmjo6zxSJqyb9wqqA5CFAwN87jWA5DzcPrzg6GZMRU>

SiteScout Goes Mobile


Demand side platform SiteScout is getting more mobile. The company has increased the amount of mobile ad inventory in its system and is showing off a number of new features to its ad-buying solution. It's promising clients more than 30 billion mobile impressions per month. "We're enabling advertisers to not only reach targeted audiences at home on their laptops and desktops, but also on the devices they take with them everywhere, like cell phones, tablets and e-readers." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMoe25oV3QTMxvwpqYK8cyIa_OfMTafIpzlwWEOjZB8ecG0MtvdcDlP4y3dFBwOC6Z9C3wNcGzKddUlV49unD4f7p6PEY-IbWzZLXiQuF-hw4IjOEI4niHKiaGuBCFvN3yRUJ-ItDQ8gx919wq7sc7kt5> . 


Pirate Ad Networks


Shiver me timbers! Jonathan Taplin, veteran film producer and director of the University of South California Annenberg Innovation Lab, thinks he's come up with a solution that's designed to hit content pirates' pocketbooks and punish brands who don't look closely at their ad environments. Taplin will produce a monthly report to shame and name brands and their advertising networks starting next year. "It is an attempt to bring a little transparency to the ad network business, which is the wild west in a weird way," Taplin tells The Drum's Stephen Lepitak. "It's not really very clear how there's an audit trail for advertisers to know where their ads are going, who's watching them...hopefully it'll be a way to bring a little clarity to that situation." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNModHX0KmWKTDbuWEyB5Fp-7qUrKHHhSgqmWB-3kwjAbZ4tfF7UoW9oTitBDCtT1jf8Mky1RaQ1IsWxv1TeSaDUd6ZIkmPxO0HpM6MwlXOhp5fGpxj5u_tDNh9bAO7jRuaImTtDwLjtaUG-Sj22W0qSotnZvMiIw8ueWvVxTakxgElv8GGQ8Q6c3B5kUhsfF1D1NbvvUbNzGxM7dHlrjcea6dpPPAA7Dn0XbIuQK5wFDuO_Qf8S4yeJRU> . 

Saving The Agency Model 

There's been a lot of hand-wringing over the past few years about how the ad agency model needs to evolve in an era of demand side platforms and greater use of earned/social media. A piece on ExchangeWire argues that agencies need to do more - and fast - as marketers begin to take "block and tackle" marketing functions in-house. And it may even be too late for some agencies says ExchangeWire: "Reckitt Benckiser have long had video buying responsibility in-housed. Kellogg's has repeatedly gone on record about working directly with Google. P&G have an extensive relationship with Audience Science. Long term, simply differentiating for the purpose of making money from media buying may not be enough." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMod0yUL4n2qIOQBZwmM-DuebvD_cBE15OuSK6EkjkG6NocsoGARFdbOSTd-IMFRH0O3cNdOfJvOvvRtLwb4Spem7bsfMFItRpysqF0J9kesZqtsGA5qETdDrr3qT4_ujNG5XHz_sjgbOresoGgJqCXXvrnV7Ae2WCApV7Qz7yt1AGYIs_VJXESKDqgNIkX-ShKEFdowpB_YsShjTsMo0T28rhn73GzPqjWq9nSHtQtGqu66EsmOPAh57ErLbaOXOLGc=> . 


To Paste, Not To Push


It's coming up on a year since social analytics company 33across bought <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMoeK6xK6mCHoBjxLoXFM0phOJQt8xAsCpgjEpQs7i6lbE-Ny9qhapEClzG6Qu4n-8s_ayf3l-6ukngYum88nJ95UdcFvdpX0dUmeRsMXKcb2LdYYxqhoomOIN7QgV_8NjVkMh608UzPjXxA0WpENDPSa>  content data provider Tynt and the two have some numbers about how plain old copy & pasting influences content sharing more than hitting a "share" button on a publisher's page. About 82 percent of sharing is done through copy & paste, with the remainder done through a share button. "The exponential rise of content sharing is often incorrectly attributed to sharing buttons on a page," said Greg Levitt, GM of Tynt's Publisher Solutions and Co-Founder of 33Across. "In reality, content sharing is caused by a far more universal user behavior: copy & paste-the most intuitive way people curate and share the exact content that they want across the web. It's surprising, but the old highlight and right click is more popular than ever." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMoea-teoxhKqEVuHokbdlzCw_4lGaweMouM1BbSGXDNnQoRhN3fgfY05GmqFkKfR8RePNlfVAzVUVyLqgN8-3SX4KOslZIMgOUpiuQKkOIdnzGP1OP9Fv6W29qRzK3Fsa2ouw2mXP7FOThQ7ius2mXMhUJElGilfQdg=> . 


'Cleaner' Google Shopping


Google began ramping up <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMoe3FErKcyhgpBBLqGq-KdbJLsdhCdRTfdsModgwQHTF-Jrnqbm5EHhreWleAvqOQnK82jJfZAy_tnGnkj_F4fCkc6h6gPy_GY5wxJZiFZCM72XGfMuNJ0AiD5Ta4xSajpFkgqHp6etDqFGP_mnDH33PBjCxPwrhBxfmgIbo14nPFqfD1KRZzYtl38JMosYeXH1cfPiZVGWzB2J8O4xtal_6e7Cf1lSVDPI=>  its e-commerce offerings this past summer and now Google Shopping is is getting its full international rollout. Still, as Sameer Samat, VP of Product Management, Google Shopping, notes, the paid product listings offerings are not done getting spruced up, as Google plans a redesigned, "cleaner" version goes up in February. The "visually cleaner results for shopping queries, including some new commercial formats on Google.com that will display products in a single unit, will replace current search results," Samat said in a blog post. "These new commercial formats will be labeled as 'Sponsored' and appear in the space currently occupied by AdWords ads." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMocFZH6-mJSo2ebZJhwCR6k0Dx6hVbs4-k8aKLbMj0P4vjX5A60d3p4M9Xfg27TdSe6SS_Ra5yqcyxNvSBlu2EH9PT7syFRDbyKHokialfXgmDOA01Hq9sv6QmJ-WgK2rt6OLs8gvAOfPe3G8eCPZ3ljDcQehQI4ezXzYeMwe22lvQ==> . Separately, Google also said that its primary AdWords product is also getting a bigger, bolder look with a new 300x600 format. Read the AdWords blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMofYt7JBFiwDfbYwvwxDb2ULFsfoaIHbzH6ITqhAbxyMKk7FJ164M3jV9Q8X3Tyg53YrhRbN1HxawtR3rkxOgbs120DrHyCKHv5Y67TFK3lCRggpt-588uOva82IKu1Oefu9Nt908Fa6OoL9yiHhQwDYKQMvYgSvpUSVm68e0H3Sqw==> .

Adding Right Media DNA


After retooling its platform and exec ranks, AdBrite says it's ready to compete with rival exchanges. A press release cites new brand safety features and says the company will innovate on price. ""We provide the air-bags without requiring you to drop a coin every time you drive the car," says new(ish) CEO Hardeep Bindra, who along with CTO Joaquin Delgado hails from Yahoo's RMX, in a press release.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016iWKzqjNMoeeqLzKO0q6qGidgFVe2zMyS243s-VMI06hbzzUyFvUK1wNn5MSceackP2cvw9tK-Ovxq6nurOV35fzzD41tZpd9qPdEeZ1iEmylSdRSk4CS-cLgauIBxGj2HJ4MCrNWxmbzA_Zfr6M7u6Y76QG_5_y> 


The Ad Climate


On MediaPost, Simulmedia's Dave Morgan steps off the conference circuit for a second to relay observations from Monaco Media Forum. About Weather Channel CEO David Kenny's presentation at MMF, Morgan says, "I was struck by how much climate change issues are being integrated into his company's strategy and mission. (...) While that may seem a perfectly logical association, there are other more subtle ways of aligning with global issues, like how newspapers functioned over the past century as a check and balance on government." Programmatic Buzz


Upstream Group's Doug Weaver comments on the recent Federated Media decision to move toward programmatic and away from its direct sales, display biz. He writes, "...there's been a thoughtful running debate for close to four years around the role of ad exchanges and programmatic channels in the publisher's world. To these thoughtful publishers, the revenue world looks like a series of dials and switches to be carefully turned and calibrated. So why the big announcement and all the breathless press coverage and Twitter chatter about Federated?" BECAUSE ADEXCHANGER SAID SO... RTB Really That Big


Put this in your acronym pipe courtesy of eMarketer: "Real-time bidding (RTB) will account for 13% of all US display advertising spending this year, more than triple its share in 2010." That's one finding from its new study on the RTB marketplace. More predictions from eMarketer: "RTB ad spending will reach $1.9 billion in 2012 as both publishers and media buyers continue to adopt RTB technology at a steady clip. Beyond 2013, growth rates will slow as the programmatic buying landscape settles and matures. Even still, by 2016, US RTB ad spending will reach $7.1 billion." Get some charts for your PPT <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANELRPLSPqdl1lf2E772n-JGZnYOildvaelLUIweg1Zp2YklUnZxJmRCIFSXz-UrrBeXPnT8Q8OsoUM7Nsodc0iN_Zkx7F78z7ce1HMUpgIKT6i0eRAd210arKWQLFMHjzv0QUVed74kZw==> . 


Facebook Feast or Famine?


Writing on his blog, App.net CEO Dalton Caldwell challenges those who accuse Facebook of throttling brands' access to their own fans. "I believe this debate is missing the big picture, and what we are in fact witnessing is the unfurling of the full-fledged Facebook business model. Facebook is showing us how they will cross the chasm from low-CTR low-CPM ad-units into what investors have been waiting for since the beginning: a Facebook analogue to Google Adwords." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANGT0yr0GHp79Hy7FUAD0WLW2LLbrPIJwqLkXCVvaDR367uroVfkIWWJ9aDR2V2O7HKS77u33pkwUnJgCIjKpfvc_PZrP_19-KSEg4kcA7eLSCc5zlhWwI2uQZZk67LWmLNeEB0Oynn_gA==>  


Agencies Not as Glum


In their Q3 earings reports last month, agency holding companies sang the blues about budget cuts and campaign cancellations -- with September being especially bad. Now they're more upbeat -- a couple of them anyway. Omnicom CEO John Wren said this at a Morgan Stanley conference yesterday: "People expect a lower growth environment across the globe, but that isn't a disaster. I am increasingly positive on 2013, especially the latter part. I'm not hearing any horrible, scary things from clients we talk to." Reuters story. Vivaki is also a little more positive. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANFJVbPCLEdVUT9nKvCoN747aVTAdfQAFzb6aZez_CtNqpiU14z6eQTNFLhDXhhzOTEbkSj1WswLYO7A1ED98TNgYccZg6Frrkvc5R7bLx3JYYUIxtFx7soB_5GIy8v2muAzaoZmdbRkO1RMbl0FCQkvncoLlO2nDDd_72TYdIYBWQ==>  


Maxing Investment


Publisher-side platform Maxifier has received more funding after announcing the investment of Dentsu's venture arm, Dentsu Digital Holdings, Inc., last month. WGI Group, comprised of Moat's Jonah and Noah Goodhart and former Right Media Exchange CEO Mike Walrath. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANGltpQ8hO7bR2AWgS8K-DgniSICqPbwiunEi28WBqHesxbBxnenaeNCyKI73k0CKN_RT1UDoHZEjbXhzonXRI9Vx8q9gvoJyQGKtBIwVuBfezgrRbS6WBXGBCiH_QmZK66s26cvbS4_l0uhgOlmDANld3iAxw5P1jHXX5EV3iRubp5ze19rn5rp6PJTRrRPtg3nHgBQnvKbEMwlr2pQbEWg0apqSdQu9JBWrLxzEnqI62qzTkoF2poTX4MxcVLTkALrkrw9goUJoQ==>  The use of Moat's ad engagement technology might enhance Maxifier's offering to inventory optimizers though there is no indication that's part of the deal. Maxifier's competitive set includes companies like Yieldex and isocket among others. 


RTB TCOS SVP


On MediaPost, Operative CEO Mike Leo is itchin' for a fight - or at least a debate. He wants to talk about all the middlemen inhibiting pricing for TCOS - True Cost Of Sale. He writes, "The TCOS for RTB can be found in all cuts taken in the middle. A typical RTB scenario may have a trading desk, DSP, exchange and SSP all taking 15% cuts. After all those cuts, a publisher whose inventory sold for $4 may only end up with 70 cents. The TCOS for that transaction: over $3." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANGmTKgQ3K9xwfAEdwjpJh5TBiMwpwZEutPjPVenoUmKLULs79doKB4w-mAmX0W7Ptwme3DSDVWJlgTvZ5Gr16cpfkYo3z3QPnRnnnKfjz6FvqreLgp__J_LvpoKMBWg_r5yi6BpHn5lyJ48Kj57ZMuXtc_qgFPhnLd15HKENavo63dlHxQ-aWHE1IVbTmjo510=>

Marketers And Consumers Disconnect


While the online ad industry bemoans the fact that marketers still spend most of their budgets on an "old" medium like TV, eMarketer points to an Adobe survey that suggests why this is still the case: TV ads are more effective. Of course, it still depends on who you ask. With respondents divided between groups of marketers and consumers, the advertisers rated online ads better than TV ads by a hair (51 percent). In comparison, roughly two-thirds of consumers said TV commercials were more effective. Who to trust? Well, if the customer's always right... Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANEBGbkyOZQFw7ZjqTu25dD96q2MddLKt4ArEbtkyioKw9avIp3Pae_KucZCtzdf8gJ4QLVQyr7tQ7lMOyC27retWTGSHPGfVqs78zcOaT52VlvvNcVySVRjHNW67jL9Gz98gix5nFMcY8khzc0Kr1wgOIvrx4dBpmPYcIE_RIa7xA==> . 


Data Doesn't Equal Wisdom


Perhaps marketers and consumers in the Adobe survey mentioned above might find more agreement with ads targeted through set-top boxes. The interactive/addressable TV ad space has been slowly gaining acceptance in the agency world the past few years. But as Alison Lowery, the CTO of targeted TV ad tech firm Simulmedia, writes in B&C, set-top box data doesn't equal wisdom about consumers. "On its own without translation and transformation, set-top box data truly helps us 'know nothing,'" Lowery says. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANFyoQNvjQOYvyjaGlq_HLy1iBYz43Onl3uDv9Z0wrgvKqOnM_hvX1Chc9PiNTdaYHttdrgtZwTOjiyUSsCSIekbJ7F6MIggwHaIpVmKuj7cIcDGffGlg36cWi1IRZ6NhoTRAVaeDDrZUKk31eKrXPS5CBAYXF6VMx4nCsntxvR54WpY8R-AL_l0> . 


IT Purchasing Gets Social


The idea of paid media always seemed a bit safer when it comes to b2b advertising. Not so anymore, as earned media/social media appears to be the key driver of what IT purchasing decisions, according to a Forrester study commissioned by professional social net LinkedIn (which has a rather obvious bias in promoting that view, it should go without saying). "85% [of IT decision makers] have used at least one social network for business purposes," notes LinkedIn marketing exec Michael Weir, adding that the stat isn't expected. "What is surprising is that 73% have engaged with an IT vendor on a social network - underscoring the value of the channel for IT marketers." Maybe so. But does that mean that LinkedIn will increase its focus on b2b marketing? That's even more unexpected. Read the blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANH4PsoHiay0l4AJ_6mrscRfWlZ8bVe1s2X3evvfDo3ea8wg79j4bLzSmoOKz-WElFWRylxM0aX85ErLh63DOnbSUFMKWdHJFio4uLDts3v5nWzUbbkXs7gs91002pHjwkj2DvQsea0h_pMOQZqD_YG2> . 


Big Measurement


You've heard of "big data." Well now sink your teeth into some "big measurement." TruEffect's Martin Smith says, "Aligning your practices to Big Measurement means focusing on key areas that contribute to the effective use of an organization's data resources: from alignment and stewardship to integration and accuracy." Read more in DM News <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TWUPQVXANG-3biTHRsHAjSyt8PkaqB_cdePWUTEYJBShvzQyZJ3aXErh5X9kJugMH6V4u4Qb6-nr1bg1h-3sJbCUR4NvQuhc7wJB9lxjGBnguQPMTNoGWV065bIAzEiM36OrmS-1oBcSvTbUMOukRLMnV_89AxqaspkwfxUptxi3xw_MXMGRQq-B4bmHWkWJmUNVfsQhmU=> .

Mobile Ad Server Heat 


Ad servers have been in limbo for the last few years, which has come as a surprise to some. To quote a recent AdWeek comment <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE1Eus-yFjDxX3pofQ1V7TNC0SB_xi27PWEQ9AbmlGf0f3nyFKmuFUUS6L3uzYuJKbMI77-q0ydsm8xhpzKp2stkvCZ2bW0gApvzFf87--ZJ5PD9jogc_dprADXdqdJyyJphYGyU82NZ7vmyC7ZY4ZBWywDZg5vUY2E=>  by Ari Paparo, alum of DoubleClick & AppNexus, "No one thought that all the ad server M&A would be largely wasted and that most efforts from these companies would be mothballed." Mobile is another story, at least for now, as Medialets yesterday announced an eight figure deal to be the mobile ad server of record for Publicis's Vivaki unit. "For Vivaki, the advantage of having a preferred ad server is being able to provide insight into the server's technological development and, in turn, use a product catered to its clients' needs." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE1xeF4CMqjgoIkKl6SdQqEhY6SrbIQDMZHgexaCltjs6A_NBICQ1-0181qDmXzWw_ORxkByunUaCyx1_fxSW97hnlurnyMxPi11E4VeKJMaZV_ZoJMFMMCfz4HgQlKeyQax7d2_uOD4FGaTQxZKNXGwFqmzKhM48rFbjEBE-mhSFyUIX8EZ6I6Tny4VytLo_8t1IIeu6OdrqnYhg6JptQAa> 

Data Coup Fails


Among the lessons to be drawn from today's ouster of McCann Worldgroup CEO Nick Brien (AdAge story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE0ACmOWbPzvPrZkLEW5MCBeYholH_2nbT_OPneKGEHi1xbLqVzYBBmvjos2lF2lbK-phePhieQJ7-6jvcBPqw4ZRaq61PAaMHtge8KMO35Ei5wSrfk3Gt3GeDfpvVHtooGcNAOFy2LBkETZ8uGfXMqRXrbhipjBA-pGeuBRw7dhCXP15A1YR8DuQW7uGtkrBTf97oodbQfYeV_bPkFi3z8N> ) is just how different are the languages spoken by media and creative. Brien came to McCann in 2010 with a strong data and media sensibility, having previously run IPG Mediabrands and before that Momentum. But the gamble didn't pay off, as the agency's creative product languished and it lost some big accounts. McCann's choice to replace Brien is Harris Diamond, known as a solid agency business guy. One spin on the shakeout is that it was a failed coup d'etat for data. Maybe it takes more than performance-driven thinking to run a global "ideas" shop. 


Gen-C Is Gen-Mobile


Most of us haven't heard of Gen-C -- Nielsen identified them <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE3Bq_t916EmOH0bCkXgZWLYl7JN1G0vK2pJqGrT8yqgmFUcfCEVRCtxO1pSgR2dbFMiH-R-dKU__qE-hootoVOrqHmrZQxGWc1g3GY8hbR0E4G8ENNPEbTYBVeWKu6acLBut2ITw8yUNSllXphIfoD8U7IFKVfPeUpW9-1IR6314-mhWp5Ds7JuNNgiTaxY8zKFyhEp6Z1Ipv_MeYI7ikar3A-ie9qGjYZ6lL21JS7okA==>  two years ago as the "connected, collective consumer" (hoo boy) -- but social media marketing provider RadiumOne has been taking the pulse of this 18- to 34-year-old cohort and it has some information on their mobile purchasing habits. "A huge percentage of people are making brand choices based on recommendations and that is really important for marketers," Kamal Kaur, RadiumOne's VP of mobile and display, told Clickz's Lisa Lacy last week. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE32qB0rg9pVx-VbgB_yXqLGtUX1-9QZEvMF_yh0W-h99kNs0D-5sCfWGVe-aDrw6OTIlHsIG5fmHDY6d1xznhOpX0z3dvPxD9y52xaYZaocA7x3z5k8jxSMUavUCi-_nH0Js0p3pphE_7MJqR8sFE8VuBFUpzazwSLjXwVKpj7ixUOqjN7Q6BNAy87Fpw8wo0_xaz4kyQqlYxgeDi-nK5g3> . Kaur added, "They have to be able to strategize their mobile presence and not treat mobile as an adjunct [phenomenon]... If they leave mobile out, it's not going to serve them well this upcoming holiday season." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE2QsZOI3onhFlT0SXyV4Wjwte_8_NFMDtzW-kOmzXz6nmDCpdlTb7iGJGKvkxehhHuxrJhzdfijXEtUiANjTXgAQGrBsEx8B-iwn4LRH8Dllj912gAgT3LFEUR315l3thxRyDA6c9oJxV9Rw9f18_Abfd0_nBMWCAqRqA-5LmWtLjD6ODrDDf8YkE2wdaAwhZ4=> . 


Tapjoy Redux


Wired's Ryan Tate picks up where Michael Arrington left off in his Sunday smackdown <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE0DW77N4nk6-x-KROBq0Xxw9-QSb-1o1jZG_CcEOCFG7iQG4XoWmigipGRRgR-3X2V7Gh7zQkKrLgNuf8Im7JTNXY5yLRVru1e3RJil36NHRHNAK64VXajttcUr1GBsUNrmJPlgB5ljzO-W8GZ50B-lf7NnrjeyD6h1evftExgbGoI5-iefShM60PuN8Yv2b914KSs-JhRg7Q==>  of mobile app incentivizer TapJoy. Tate notes Apple may struggle to police mobile installs as stakes rise in the app space and the paid install market goes underground. "Apple's guidelines are all well and good, but $60 million tends to be far more interesting to your average entrepreneur. To win this fight, Apple's app store enforcers are going to need a lot more muscle." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE3u0zuDOGMfqy38HTEF6Mspj_Q0SoCMGI0iN_xditUv3qRSVcTJO9vBDFck2ZGm8oEKNmLWDI-ZjSnadfjs8pwGEdfMP2VdVgaQykH4SZ1vUv4DWlrZZeTzxryVIa3_Z3Y92e1fjX6jrqtxGdewxkqng2JXDEzpcBHi3JN2lh3auU3Q6wPkhBzo9iy2anYw8_29EGJhPtScRfPnwgjgwHAwRj9DUloqrbFMcUhenAn_oeGcTNLd5N3TbFu0LLXqAXryjV_Ly-wACLIwwgMQEwH-cUF5YZy4-7CFrU6NEDfqiT-G445vn47eQCpkZGT92YAiiXdhqJQvlmtFrWi1pF9fnOTPO9MDACo=>  


Tumblr Meets Mad Men


Now that we're all satisfied with Facebook's and Twitter's evolving advertising programs, we can turn our attention to the other micro-blog service without a clear revenue model: Tumblr. The company has assembled a dozen ad agency and tech providers in its "A-List Partnership Program." Adweek's Chris Heine likens it to Facebook's Preferred Developer Program. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001V84-Pf-ILE2yn9bfWbccVxhogeQMzehkd9Byo1Tvkfb7COLP8g4VLsrVRnqDNXiW4druRsSakivs5icAgUfKj6gQFG0XnOHFPZh2jnQB2H5XE0Fr3xrR13k7W4GYTWDfxX64n8GfpAGsGWPDgq9NveJSG1mhZJkilXthKVO8rcoLPI0O9afQPlrnaXbE57q9> . Rick Webb, marketing and revenue lead at New York-based Tumblr, said in a statement: "We couldn't be happier with the early success brands have had using Tumblr to tell their stories, and we've been honored to work with some of the most creative and talented agencies around the world."

No Joy In AppVille


Is Tapjoy's "incentivized" mobile app world crashing down? While Apple has practically kicked out apps that offer users incentives such as virtual currency in exchange for downloading a marketplace for games, Tapjoy and its brethren have largely moved to HTML5. But not being a part of Apple's iOS has cut into revenues of Tapjoy and its partners, writes Techcrunch's Mike Arrington, who slashes and burns through the company's business model. "I can't wait to see what Tapjoy does next in this ever-escalating arms race," says Arrington. "One thing's for sure - it'll be very profitable. And very shady." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zzJ1lFDaqcDUrToCj8qWukRDVAmVjuIX67Ni_5CK4tIJwebKwTaCjvdErlTxeGz2es4iZud_CF35Uo0mGzUSHAm4iR-L-_HwjT5kMQdiKhJ2J__p4MTgq3l2M0V3BSDBiPIR6BFZXGH1tBYpttAi9PGT42keQtBx-NhjTrPku4EHBskM10T4WSakxdL50EkukneeEJYQupgGQ==> .


Anti-Trust Decision Nears


The U.S. Federal Trade Commission (FTC) may be close to giving Google an "ultimatum" in regards to the FTC's anti-trust investigation of the company. Bloomberg's Sara Forden writes, "For almost 20 months, the FTC has been probing whether Mountain View, California-based Google is abusing its dominance of the Internet, and it's prepared to sue if the operator of the world's largest search engine fails to make an acceptable proposal." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zyyKrMblgn6H2v7hYp-T-X8F6anfHthy_SdZ08e_JzoyJWvOqBFE-RmkNCGkQwDvnoaLFV3-1JmMxrN_wddrCKmqbd-LJZtccNvRiBjkNKZel2pEQ6dMN5TrMDs7cTd4uoxnKl03PL74sxwNMyhUPak8117sckBpW2OxBeq3nHPQDiqE_RAlTgyka99Vn5Rlueu6sBFRdHd5kl9wYc0U8DY> . 


Buying Into Marketing Services


In Ad Age, Kate Kaye reports on last week's Epsilon acquisition of Hyper Marketing's brand agency Ryan Partnership, its social agency SolutionSet and its retail agency Catapult . Kaye writes, "The idea here is to marry Epsilon's consumer data insights and data management and analysis capabilities with HMI's marketing services." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zx_r7LykhmfozNYrwsmYyjSwZTkCS7QvEBR9cr8AKTBb6VtfkLnJkY_PTMP9J1YkwSi66GbhgTPrHg85s7JQQ3p4kjjYjTGtUyHtckWyHpUFYzSLC5nHuVaZHkKNvH1TzWEg8qVcolrl89E_AElEEEB9VKCAvhTBOSLVnrJZmBUkvG3udA8MyOAAoKElWxIfRWcxon6AU1iH1vBwa0o56kV>  Experian and Acxiom also offer various flavors of marketing services among other big, data-focused players in the marketing space. 


Agency Ups and Down


We recently noted  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zzPpOtUyP84dc0AvYhfKmzvR__x0EFj1bNC72NrkCGa5vTHOVpAKN3VsxvhEk8P90x-9s7Wr2cx2s0bbTnAuWW0562RlAt9s_VIXsKMfuMLKEihoEUge74SnX75TsPNoGAtPta_IfK661qKmzUg-jUL8DRWXoLniFjxQDUURbcyyWdNIlGjt398G9tn9YgKscXd-tj5-fFxhxofQEAfQ6vN6MsB9A32CU0=> September was a surprisingly dismal month for agency holding companies. Turns out October was a little brighter for at least one of them as Publicis saw 7% organic growth led by the U.S. "At this point in time, we cannot yet confirm that growth and confidence are back," CEO Maurice Levy told Reuters in a statement. "Europe and analog media are still at worrying levels." Read a little more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zyXYnp4nDG5zvGGhZVy0jYFQ_DQcmZKjPUCnMafHc7Il7qtUbWnzcmmRvSOhFXtWa_ZeTG_eaUfdUKVgq6zetoSLdpsBCbgjsmAmtX-Ru5xOuS3zCc9c509kJ0Y7-qO-HYlkO1N2yWjpwegtbdnQBzBw2Kv5AvwUG0PwehWb6uxpnhaAqGchobS>  


Adblock, the Dongle


Can the ad blocking micro-industry make the jump from browser plugins to hardware? A new device (in development) called AdTrap promises to remove ads from websites, audio streams, video and mobile apps. So far it's raised about half its $150,000 goal, and all signs point to "go." "We have parts on hand to build 25 AdTrap's right now... Everything should be shipped by February 2013." Read more and see pics. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zynI4U6whGimvnrCL72OuQRZDoaLizuzufOGZLRPrjOJGn8XZMKuIMfNl8KWdkHZA4CP2nIHUOXJgql84shXLh4hjlDxesZOQrGCG08wTmG_2shvShssyH12DYJ7xsd8BAABHFqgVyZwIXqg7RkQOa9Mq8oAm1RJzJEnqjoL55wWtUvrNDP7Zlu>

Thumbs On Display


Q&A site maker Stack Exchange announced that it's embedding a widget in its standard display media - courtesy of ad serving system AdZerk - that provides for a thumbs up or down on ads. Stack Exchange's Kourneel Boman writes, "We want you to only see ads you want to see, which in turn means that our advertisers will only advertise to people who are actually interested in what they have to sell (which is sort of the holy grail of display advertising)." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zyIgo3c3csZFXBioV2HCmisOk45hNcrfgNRQsXfbNAMJ9SpNqYlwiBGoyRhgOHE2tT26Xs85YJKeD6h4-pJeZj_WmLbA0xMjjcr1-9wpeExJ00NUMTBO3IgZEKx1x1b6h3c3-vzLevJxSttxJYD3MFMknXaBEXCzCijy-7AJNaGlwMwilM-0w4s8ip5uUY9ehh7W7w0_SxI4BvgqD1vrMiq> 


Channel Changer


TV ratings may be the least precise form of measurement in entire media landscape. But television advertising is still where the money is. And while the model isn't broken, that doesn't mean that the industry is as solid as it once was. Rho Ventures partner Doug McCormick, writing in GigaOm, says that the industry doesn't have to wait for a long slide to employ "smarter, online-style tech" to better target ads will benefit both networks' and marketers' bottom line. "Agencies must start managing media spends to develop specific sales forecasts for items or services that their clients are marketing, while ensuring that they deliver the target users at the most efficient price," McCormick says. "The agency/media equation should not stop with the delivery of tonnage audiences. It needs to take the next step." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zy9NPbRHeBkmKY1Q92rTuDN5qrDO1lVJQKG3jv1Ar8W0tfpVzOw68dlHIIS-_Y56SGPTSuy2teHm6-KVdbWIG7kYR6e9kGy8EFSUpam2QaGyWHUIZuP_bvqmKGwjlDeQpbblFC-358-umWlef9Z_oG2ffgRotDx7mHRY_H2t9Tm4Q3mK3_RsDyfTElXeD6_rOkkIDJ9taOwEA==> . 


Programmatic Brand


On Forbes, Kellogg's digital marketer, Bob Arnold, talks about programmatic buying and the brand. He says, "We've seen tremendous results when using programmatic buying. Depending on the brand, the digital media ROIs have increased as much as six times, according to our 3rd party market mix models. Compared to two years ago, we're aggressively leveraging it today." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zzLJlIrZuuotfJE1vHp989XWzt1ltVkthGzhaWyiSVFnEyTm8eEIoLSOuvQsXEPwRSmfK92y8_zf6PUZ6yBrrAt_rt5yDVoCtAuM7ZIlS8npDfAmivU_dtqFQNYfysXl_J9s4-UJuptc74ipqm6Zsu9h7d-_UYKpjRY5uM1dwlX2jS62yyf_FN7-DgLf9F23a6lhRWENINjP_ez6uuzh0p0ec2Ey2Iqrfc=>  


Future TV Network


In Ad Age, Michael Learmonth does not report that Google remains fully committed to producing its own content and putting the television networks out of business. But, he does say that Google is starting to compete for TV budget and continuing to invest in content on YouTube. Is this the Connected TV network of the future? Learmonth quotes Google/YouTube's Global Head of Content Strategy Jamie Byrne, "Our biggest objective was to kick-start the [YouTube] ecosystem, to bring in great creators, to deepen our relationships with advertisers and to grow viewership." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rN4hnaPf_zzPHwmmwaWjbTQfTtfmQq4LmAz40JlitcspdmSbzsSPVYEOcmEDk98u1LCe-ge3r3CgViuIQDD5UBA_3s8VeRm2sZ9-zhNwLc0UoVU4uAcHlj7JGpX_du_BgWph9DYHCmjqJRSPaFpkmZSIHBEIQvGDocRvb87eQYWuYmauqVynwqLVIumM4PfOwbZTrHIe6QU=>

DG Break-Up Imminent?


DG, acquirer of MediaMind <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul8DhVf0q5thnRzA-o0zY3v5GZg_SCV1EgYI7Kc0gEMGyhdejLbIVMcZ76vnHrSgUfK4Fj5S1lCKyFejkoeDrnP6udf5lp1ZBpY3Uzn2Z37P-igUqZnQ8CDyc794p19itGJIoN_CLMoUBKPIL8mjeIxyeHfDHmwt9UcI6avb5zU7iAsYM6LWGvQljupdNWFF6PC1nUwpHpEYsQ==> , Peer39 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul_31sJ_gP2iqqsS15FBheQs4AVYcNxSsaBgUJO4SCM0uNjrGvZXOxxOY1qOBC8bS2FoURGDcx2LF2cz_9FGRgjntCkKdeSRHKEOthejlxH9joQwseI2ZCCilNeqkx1FEM07lMJySKHR6uF9MLpum0wo> , Eyewonder and Unicast among others, announced its third quarter 2012 results last Thursday. The company's TV unit reported flat results (with continued competition from Extreme Reach) as did online on an "organic" basis ($33.7 million in revs). Later on the earnings call, CEO Neil Nguyen cited price compression. Even though the online group sold 40% more impressions of standard display and rich media, it didn't make up for pricing decrease (hence the flat results). Also, DG raised a white flag of sorts with the dreaded "writedown." From the release: <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul-a690xKJBk9O7Qsd0eLKnHJdA88AOdL7Pn1_zybl5EgtAgL5xkxSKMVUbMA5jMz5Kx2HjW7amSd0nAjpTQEoYLpVSKwfq3YCEmLXXWGziz23yMu_uUZOlT3SBVZrOqwSK-W-22Tm5IHd4w0akEJ1mqq2jMOam6UXsP5jz6WtiEkacNskHAp_fYWQsfO3G9O2AnZ18KLjUga0LcNoP9BQxj>  "DG's third quarter operating results include a $208.2 million non-cash charge before income taxes related to the write-down of our online reporting unit's goodwill." Also, the company has a new CFO and the strategic review of the company remains ongoing meaning that the company could be sold or perhaps parts spun off. The online group is a juicy apple for some company out there -- or maybe as a standalone. 

More earnings call highlights... CEO Neil Nguyen noted a big $57 million, 3-year customer contract for MediaMind from an "EMEA agency." Outgoing CFO Omar Chouir said that the online group has about 675 employees (1,675-ish total for the company). Also, Nguyen complemented former Peer39 CEO Andy Ellenthal for the turnaround on the sales side from previous quarters for the online group. Read the earnings transcript on Seeking Alpha <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul_cbdr59QD1125AKTw_bH8QC7J-m03Xy5gVhPB_G_3MBtdz27ds2DB4ifCDZC8afEGOyuPHNr8cw3TfGKxm5-t1D2wAim-9BphwHCp2KLcN-rPPwET4mEtpiM4IIEWGDawDmc411i8m0YqMU8TpdPM-rN3B7MaJB5BXqSvB3iH9tfxAnXlZZblAwuwCeztmGikvg4awFuy-yGjevjzdief6AqCKwqoN49HdOie4AQdTCw==> . Oh, it's great being public, isn't it? In spite of it all, the acquisition rumors helped buoy the stock price <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul_2lrQCGqCZrDzmpaVFWn6Irf4064XSlpVJRC9DmT5pSLBxULOVTggsTHeaxQNeT1PW5eULVOmeCzGXetShxj6YeDmzVTVfb5OKfSBiSn2l4vWNpvwm61NNOq6DnvPSFy4aB-OtaT3idmgICfKtvGb9Egf5mV2RbHg=>  by nearly 20% on Friday. 


Refreshing Trends


Piper Jaffray analyst Gene Munster has his team busy refreshing the Yahoo home page everyday as they collect data on Yahoo display trends. Barron's quotes the outcome of Munster's lastest "refresh": "On a daily basis, we check the display ads on Yahoo!'s home page to determine if ads are higher CPM guaranteed placements (sold by Yahoo!'s sales team) or performance ads supplied by an ad network or another third party. For the month of October, 74% of the ads we observed were guaranteed compared to 58% last October and 89% in September.. (...)" He remains neutral on Yahoo prospects. Read a bit more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul9fDMlxjGMNy9-PrLsWMbABYowPvvf3iPHWZlKA3xWDoyOchx-hFTG1tMcqJrwGnNIY-md4KJuG3iVKsieFaVcddO3LerByZx9y4wjcQUbNEy4tlfrNRSPs8eWky16caLtaETcq832-hK-JmuNqX5bzh5nauxhczfgOVa8wchK-1lpnvXbF4lV20nFhRQtP8mIFliDCehHDnbKNd2gtPUjVgMBpkT-JjvYp-EQ0kf9VzA==>  


Federated Goes Programmatic


The Next Web, a Federated Media partner, reports that the direct sold, display ad business that was once the mainstay of Federated's site rep empire is being mothballed in 2013. The Next Web's Brad McCarty writes, "In fact, FM has reduced its staff by 24 people who were on the direct sales side, and hopes to add at least 40 more programmatic positions in 2013." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul8c_AJL5gyHp7G84xINJ5HHex5FoqJ6R7O06STCedcl2lkRWfMQSyD2DgRvPfK1gjDDagHE0Qap71EVMexwjl1bbY632tYhQObCNi6apjAghR-CBVzSC9pFRbTYzkYOrHTsVNOKyY9n9r7p4LFCGlCJeH6hwNVfLnsAdOIxErTZqBDkMpGyXPmjTELHOnjf8zMnvv_2T_OUc27bXiCNLLWJkIQe6LJEaDiDM7_Rk3hUnpeFz0T9F0bcJ-DsgMHIkswO831vnary8A==>  


The Facebook Circular


New research on Facebook's impact on voting behavior has clear potential for retail, writes Blinq Media CEO Dave Williams in an AdAge column. "Physical stores still account for 93 percent of total sales, and circular ads have historically been retail's biggest tool for bringing consumers into stores. Retailers have been looking for a digital way to drive foot traffic." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul-X3ZLOgliUeSAwt0TNlH38SpdkoKO6u_6cjKXn7wwi-zfXoJkXwLqBax53XF36idAGFdoet2FigamzfPco-SDV_ZxGcYGQ9jCTMCaoD-d4VgTcBCG1f0jHBsY1hQRy2KYOGuVQTjM2KZKG_vXmz1ED86oW6LhpZVE8OoMpaGdZY4qD2inyzKvuykusicKnmsR2Fg_9eYqVKjJXMlzLHZJP>  


Location Smarts


Hyperlocal pub StreetFight peeks under the hood of some new location analytics tech from mobile ad net xAd. "SmartLocation uses an algorithm to analyze a slew of consumer location signals, such as latitude and longitude...IP address, zip code and city/state address. Once obtained, the data is scored for accuracy - to ensure that LL coordinates, if available, are real and not converted from a zip code, via geocoding software, which can lead to imprecise data - and performance." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001neas6cE8Ul8vJhlmODLp1aoZrAD_YtkQeCZR7vbXGVUEBC4tpA2k9BzYJXNTJgrsURpzNb10pSB4wSvqcie-pyxlb_bTpKCTsRVuQoeKTyXofaH9fftP8XxRO5X6qf1TS2j44wFHYa-UHLi8om49aYzpySZ5V8IUqN4uRQ4g1UxIf3pB1IYPxIk9lfrQi6BIiMngyHOcXxqetiUDcId6q2-7l6v77gSlGrNAYGocUl4_Nkg6bypS-w==>
